Collection of Fishery Development Fee Still Awaiting Mediation 139

Deputy Director Added to Construction Fee Collection Office

Official from the Ministry of Industry Appointed to Serve, Having Assumed Office Yesterday

The dispute over the collection of fishery development fees by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fishery Improvement Association has been delayed for months without resolution. The reasons held by both sides are extreme. In order to clarify the truth, the New News Agency reporter inquired from all parties and recorded the information obtained as follows:

Collection Methods 140

Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, in order to develop the fishing industry, in addition to opening up saline resources, and to eliminate pirates and subsidize national defense, based on the principle of "taking from fishing and using for fishing," organized the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fishery Improvement Association and determined the collection methods for fishery development fees. The fees collected are to be collected by the fish markets and stored in a special account, and a weather forecasting plan for important fishery locations in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang area is to be implemented at any time, and patrol ships are to be added to protect the safety of the fishing industry at sea.

Motivation for Opposition 141

Since its establishment, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fishery Improvement Association's construction fee collection office began collecting fees on April 15th, and divided the area into ten districts due to the vastness of the jurisdiction. The collection of fishery products is divided into five categories: ㈠ fresh fish, ㈡ salted fish, ㈢ dried fish, ㈣ marinated fish, ㈤ shellfish. The collection standard is 1% of the value, deducted by the fish markets and submitted. However, the collection personnel have been harassing and demanding various unreasonable amounts that are not stipulated in the regulations, and even fractional amounts are calculated as whole numbers. Also, shellfish and other categories have always been imported goods, and customs duties have already been collected by the customs at the time of import. The construction fee collection office is collecting construction fees again. Therefore, the fish industry groups in Hangzhou Zhaishan, Ningbo, Shipu, Dinghai, Zhenhai and other places, in order to avoid pain, have risen up to oppose the organization of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fish Industry United Company to form a banner and negotiate with the Improvement Association.

Three Mediations 142

In order to avoid misunderstandings between the two sides, Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo specially invited Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, and Yu Zuoting to mediate twice with Meng Lujiu and other representatives of the Fish Industry United Association. At that time, the opinions of the two sides were not completely consistent, so the various misunderstandings of the past still need to be explained. It is heard that Du and others still need to mediate a third time in order to resolve the matter.

Suspension of Fee Collection 143

Before the two sides reach a resolution, only 5 of the 25 fish markets in the city have paid the fees, while the rest have suspended payment. Therefore, the construction fees collected by the collection office are very small. The salaries of the staff have not been paid for nearly three months. The director of the office, Dai Yongtang, has personally advanced more than 10,000 yuan for office expenses. The 2,000 yuan in operating expenses per month promised to subsidize the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fishery Administration has not been allocated at all. Therefore, as of now, all fees have been suspended, and the work is also at a standstill.

Sending Assistance 144

Dai Yongtang, the director of the construction fee collection office, is from Zhenhai. He was originally the general affairs director of the Ice and Fresh Industry Association. Since taking office, he has been strongly opposed by all parties, and his attitude has been quite passive. He has also been deeply saddened by the various harassments of the staff in various districts. The Ministry of Industry has become aware of these difficulties and has specially appointed Luo Yonghu, a specialist committee member from Guangdong, as the deputy director of the construction fee collection office to assist in all matters. It is learned that Mr. Luo has arrived in Shanghai by the Beijing-Shanghai train and assumed office yesterday.

Future Predictions 145

According to the New News Agency reporter's inquiries from all parties, the Ministry insists on collecting 1% of the construction fees and will not allow changes. The fish merchants have consistently opposed the collection of construction fees. However, in order to seek construction expenditures for the fishery industry and protect the safety of the fish merchants at sea, the Ministry can open up new avenues and collect a certain amount of ocean protection fees, which can be done in reality. Fortunately, the mediators have considerable relationships with each other, and it is expected that this major storm may come to an end after three mediations.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Marine Engineers to Submit Request to the Company Again Today, Willing to Take the Exam 146

| But Refuse Foreign Examiners and Must Set New Salary Increase Method |

More than 80 marine engineers from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Jianghai vessels are planning to submit a request to the company again today, after the company replied with two methods regarding the request for a salary increase. The content roughly states that China has never had a marine engineering school, so most of the marine engineers are uneducated. However, they have more than ten years of experience, so the exam may not be a problem. However, they refuse to be examined by foreigners, and the company must set the salary increase method after passing the exam and stipulate that the exam should be held twice a year to give those who fail a chance. Currently, the vessels have not yet returned to Shanghai, so a reply will be made after all the marine engineers have unanimously agreed.

Heshun Wharf Dispute Resolved 147

Five Measures Signed

The Heshun Wharf in Pudong was recently leased to the Zhongxing Company Guangzu Warehouse. The failure to properly accommodate the old workers caused public outrage and led to a dispute. Representatives were sent to seriously negotiate with the authorities of the Zhongxing and Heshun companies, and a request was submitted to the Party and government agencies for assistance. At 9 AM yesterday, the Bureau of Social Affairs summoned both parties to the bureau for mediation. Wu Yaoting and Li Bingfa from the labor side, foreman Zhang Dehua, Long Peiyun representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Wang Guoxian representing the Public Security Bureau attended. The meeting was chaired by Wang Gang from the Bureau of Social Affairs, with Wang Zhiqin as the recorder. After both parties stated their reasons, five solutions were immediately formulated as follows: ㈠ The original full-shift foreman will continue to be hired by Zhang Dehua. ㈡ The original full-shift foreman should obey the instructions of foreman Zhang Dehua and Ling Qishuang in assigning the command of running the wharf. ㈢ If Zhang Dehua needs to dismiss the original foreman due to major misconduct, he should first submit it to the Bureau of Social Affairs for approval before dismissing. ㈣ The original workers will continue to work as usual under the leadership of the original full-shift foreman. ㈤ Foreman Zhang Dehua will handle the treatment of the foreman and workers as usual. With the agreement of both parties, a resolution was announced.

Spring Cocoon Car Transport from Zhejiang Ends, Summer Cocoons Begin 148

The car transport of spring cocoons produced in various parts of Zhejiang Province via the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway this year has now concluded. It is understood that this cocoon transport has always been undertaken by the Huitong Transportation Company under a special contract with the Railway Bureau. Therefore, this year the company continued to handle the transport, with cocoons being loaded at various stations and transported to Shanghai. This ended at the end of June. In total, only 54,500 packages of spring cocoons were unloaded at the North and South stations. In recent years, silk prices have been steadily declining, and factories have been reducing or ceasing production. Consequently, the amount of cocoon transport has decreased year by year. Compared to last year's total of around 120,000 packages, this year's figure is down by six-tenths. It is also learned that summer cocoons in various parts of Zhejiang Province have also been launched on the market and weighing has commenced. Purchase prices for summer cocoons are the same as for spring cocoons. Chang'an was the earliest area. Yesterday, the first batch of summer cocoons was reported for loading by the Huitong Company at Chang'an Station. These were purchased by the Shanghai Wuxing Silk Factory: 178 packages of summer cocoons, 116 packages for Yu Tai, and 129 packages for Rui Yu. All were transported to the South Station for unloading and delivery. It is said that the total number of summer cocoons this year is approximately five or six thousand packages.

Tobacco Merchants Petition for the Abolition of the Special Tax on Native Tobacco Leaves 150

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the Ministry of Finance recently announced regulations for the special tax on native tobacco leaves. Starting from July 1st of this year, the old public sales fee will be abolished and replaced with a special tax. Native tobacco leaves produced in the seven provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Fujian will be subject to a special tax of 4.15 yuan in national currency per 100 market catties net weight, collected in one lump sum. Subsequently, transportation and sale within the seven-province area will not be subject to further taxation, etc. Local tobacco merchants believe that the tobacco leaf business has plummeted in recent years. While the reasons are not limited to one factor, the high cost and the inability to raise prices are indeed important reasons. The high cost is primarily due to the heavy tax rates and transportation costs. This has caused tobacco merchants to hesitate to move forward. Even if they purchase tobacco leaves, there is no profit to be made, and the accumulation of tobacco leaves in the producing areas prevents them from being shipped out, causing difficulties for both tobacco merchants and farmers. This impact already existed during the old public sales fee era. Although the newly promulgated special tax is an improvement over the public sales system, the tax rate is too high, and tobacco merchants and the people cannot bear the burden. The local Tobacco Leaf Industry Association has repeatedly received reports of difficulties from its members and has submitted a petition to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, requesting that the special tax on native tobacco leaves be temporarily suspended to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Meanwhile, representatives Huang Fuqing, Wang Zuoting, Zhuang Zhikuan, and the acting chairman of the association, Hua Daxiu, have been dispatched to Nanjing to petition the government. Furthermore, a letter from the Secretariat of the Legislative Yuan to the Shanghai-Ningbo-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Association Joint Association stated: "Greetings, A document forwarded by the President of the Yuan has been received, regarding the Tax Administration's preparation to illegally collect taxes on native tobacco and alcohol, requesting prompt prevention, etc. Approved: Noted. Since the document has been submitted, please await instructions from the relevant administrative authorities. The original document is sent to the Finance Committee of this Yuan for reference, etc. In addition to forwarding it, this letter is to inform you for your reference. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai-Ningbo-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Association Joint Association, Secretariat of the Legislative Yuan, June 30th."

Shop Assistant Commits Suicide by Poison After Being Discovered Embezzling Funds 151

Huang Jinfu, a native of Pudong, aged 21, was a shop assistant in the Changhe Rice Shop on Niuzhuang Road. His behavior was undisciplined, and he was habitually idle. As a result, his monthly income was all spent on extravagance. Recently, he secretly took dozens of yuan from the shop's account and spent it on entertainment. The shop owner, seeing his lavish spending, secretly investigated and reviewed the accounts. He discovered that dozens of yuan were missing and questioned Huang. Knowing that he could not deny it, Huang confessed and promised to return the money immediately. However, Huang's family was poor and could not afford such an amount. Desperate, he privately checked into the Shanghai New Hotel at the Daxin Street intersection yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. and committed suicide by taking poison. He was discovered by a tea server at the hotel, who reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. Patrolman No. 808 transported him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of the poisoning, he died at 6 p.m. The hospital sent the body to the coroner's office for examination.

Examination of Murdered Female Corpse at Wusong Zhonggong School 152

Newspapers Lined Underneath the Body

Date of Incident Not Very Recent

Regarding the discovery of a murdered female corpse in the destroyed dormitory of the China Public School in Wusong, which was reported in yesterday's newspaper, we now have more detailed information to continue reporting. The corpse was wearing a purple floral-patterned qipao made of free cloth, with a white cotton long vest underneath, grey cotton shorts, and bare feet, wearing blue saving shoes. Beside the body was only a powder box, with no other belongings. There was an injury to the head of the corpse, with blood covering the ground. Underneath the corpse was a June 29th Shanghai Times newspaper, indicating that the incident likely occurred on the evening of June 29th. Beside the corpse were several pieces of food such as bread and preserved plums, suggesting that a love affair had gone wrong, leading to the tragic murder. It is unknown whose daughter she was. The local bailiff has reported the case to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau and the Shanghai District Court for investigation. Yesterday afternoon at 3 p.m., the District Court dispatched Prosecutor Xie Lian to Wusong for examination. The examination determined that the corpse died from injuries. The bailiff, Pu Yousheng, was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial, pending identification by family members.

Gao Lis Retracts Daughter from Gao Ronghai 153

Gao Li, a woman from Changzhou, is currently 39 years old. She has a daughter named Xiangmei, who is 19 years old and quite attractive. Due to poverty at home, she brought her daughter to Shanghai several years ago, renting a room in Yangshupu. Her daughter found work at the Dacheng Yarn Factory, where she earned a meager living. Recently, she met Gao Ronghai, a fellow villager who works at the Sensen Optical Factory in Hongxing Lane at the end of Yu Xing Road. Seeing that Xiangmei was somewhat attractive, he had bad intentions. He falsely claimed that working in the factory was too hard and that he could introduce her to work at the Ximen Maoge Factory, where she could earn 40 to 50 yuan per month. Gao Li, seeing the potential profit, did not suspect him. On the morning of the 16th of last month around 10 a.m., he pretended to help send her to work at the Maoge Factory and took Xiangmei away, but she did not return for several days. The mother went to Gao Ronghai to negotiate, asking him to return her daughter. He initially agreed to delay for three days. When she went to negotiate again, Gao Ronghai instead gathered a dozen unemployed vagrants and went to Gao Li's home, where they committed assault. The woman was alert and escaped, reporting it to the Fourth Police Station of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau. The police arrested Ronghai. The others involved in the assault fled when they saw things were not going well. After being detained, Ronghai admitted that he would hand over Xiangmei within a week. However, he still did not return the girl by the deadline. Yesterday, Li personally apprehended Ronghai and handed him over to the Zhabei Judicial Section. She also hired a lawyer to draft a complaint to the District Court Prosecutor's Office, accusing Gao Ronghai of inducing a minor for illicit purposes, under Article 257, Sections 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law, requesting punishment, and requesting the Judicial Section to approve the transfer of Gao Ronghai to the District Court for questioning.

Xu Hongqing Inflicts Private Punishment and Assaults His Concubine 154

丨Sentenced to a Fine of Forty Yuan丨

Xu Hongqing, from Yancheng, opened a pancake shop at 374 Yuanfang Road. He married a woman surnamed Mou in his hometown. Two years ago, he cohabitated with Wang Suzhen (25 years old), a woman from his neighborhood, in the shop, as if they were husband and wife. Recently, Suzhen suddenly changed her behavior, often going to listen to local opera and watch movies, and playing mahjong. Xu repeatedly tried to dissuade her, but she refused, so he rebuked her. At the beginning of last month, Xu returned to his hometown for business and only returned to Shanghai on the 26th. He learned that Suzhen had been away for three nights. Xu questioned her harshly. She claimed that she had been out watching a play and it was late, so she stayed at a little sister's place. Xu was furious and stripped Suzhen of her clothes, tied her hands and feet with iron chains, beat her severely with a wooden stick, and locked her in the bedroom, preventing her from leaving. She cried for help, but no one responded. She could only wash her face with tears every day. A neighbor anonymously reported the incident to the police. Detective Liu Zhongcheng was immediately ordered to arrest Xu Hongqing and rescue Wang Suzhen, along with the iron chains. The incident was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court for questioning by Judge Wu Zehan. The police lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, explained the situation, stating that the victim, Wang Suzhen, had been examined by a doctor and found to have suffered severe injuries to her body and legs, with medical certificates as proof. He then presented the wooden stick and iron chains for inspection. The defendant confessed to having an affair with Suzhen, but denied the rest of the story, stammering. Wang Suzhen testified that she had been severely beaten by the defendant and did not want to go back. Judge Wu reviewed the testimony and sentenced Xu Hongqing to a fine of 40 yuan as a warning.

Monk Killed by Car 155

Yesterday afternoon at 5:30 p.m., when the Shanghai-to-Beijing express train on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway was passing through the Wangjiajing area of Tanziawan in Zhabei, a man dressed in a grey kasaya, wearing black monk shoes and grey socks, about 25 years old and resembling a monk, was walking beside the track. The driver of the train saw him and honked the horn as a warning, but it was too late. He was knocked down, and his head was bleeding profusely. Nearby patrol officers rushed to investigate and found that he had already died. They reported it to the Fourth District Headquarters. Since no family members of the deceased could be found, a local bailiff was assigned to guard the body, pending a report to the court for examination.

Shen Mengyi Safely Rescued from Kidnappers Amidst a Rain of Bullets 157

Kidnappers' Den Located on Avenue Joffre, Adjacent to the French Park

Eleven Kidnappers, Including Men and Women, Apprehended

丨Mengyi Says He Was Treated Well in the Kidnappers' Den丨

On the morning of the 20th of last month at 8:55 a.m., a kidnapping occurred in front of the Jianghai Customs Library on Xinza Road in the Public Concession. The victim was Shen Mengyi, the eldest son of the renowned Huzhou silk merchant Shen Tianxin. The details have been reported in this newspaper for three weeks. It was not until yesterday that Hua Detective You A’gen of the Lao Zha Police Station obtained a clue. Subsequently, at around 5 p.m., he, along with Chinese and Western detectives from the French Police, raided the kidnappers' den at 559 Avenue Joffre, rescued the hostage on the spot, and apprehended eleven kidnappers, including men and women. The kidnappers opened fire and resisted arrest, resulting in a shootout with over thirty shots fired. As a result, two kidnappers were shot and wounded. The kidnapping and rescue details are explored and recorded below.

The Shen Family 158

Shen Tianxin, a wealthy silk merchant from Huzhou residing in Shanghai, is currently 52 years old and lives in Building No. 10 of No. 493 Lane on Seymour Road (i.e., Zizai Li). In 1927, Shen served as the Superintendent of the Suzhou Customs, further enhancing his reputation. Before long, he tired of his position and retired to Shanghai, where he continued to focus on his old business, while also engaging in large-scale real estate transactions. Shen has two sons and two daughters. The eldest son is named Mengyi, aged 25. The eldest daughter is named Yiyao, aged 23. Mengyi is currently an employee in the Foreign Exchange Department of the Bank of China on the Bund. Yiyao works at the Jianghai Customs Library on Xinza Road.

Mengyi's Kidnapping 159

The Shen family owns a car, Concession No. 2085. On the morning of the 20th of last month at 8:55 a.m., Shen's brother and sister boarded the car to go to work, with the chauffeur Zhu Guangfeng driving. As Zhu brought Yiyao to the Customs Library at No. 1714 Xinza Road, Yiyao got out of the car, and Mengyi was kidnapped by four kidnappers and taken away, disappearing without a trace. Shen's car was later discovered near Rihui Port that evening, but it was empty, and there was no sign of anyone.

Ransom Negotiations 160

After the case occurred, the Concession police authorities took it very seriously and ordered their subordinates to solve the case within a specified time. However, the kidnappers were very cunning and maintained close contact with the hostage's family, preventing the police from intervening. It is said that the initial demand was very high. After several rounds of negotiations, the kidnappers agreed to a minimum ransom of 80,000 yuan. Although Shen was wealthy, he was unwilling to part with such a large sum, so the matter was delayed and no deal was reached. Until yesterday afternoon at around 5 p.m., Hua Detective You A’gen of the Lao Zha Police Station suddenly received a tip-off, stating that the hostage in the case was being held at 559 Avenue Joffre. He was requested to arrest them quickly.

Raiding the Kidnappers' Den 161

After receiving the tip, Detective You immediately joined Western Detective Robert, Hua Detectives Liu Junqing, Zhou Guisheng, Su Changsheng, and the general team, and traveled by car to report to the French Police Special Agency. Inspector Jin Jiulin, Chief Detective Zhang Ziying, Deputy Chief Detective Zhou Yaoting, along with detectives Cai Jinzhang, Qin Youyu, Zhang Chunsheng, Yang Jiaxue, Geng Quanchang, Xu Guilin, and Western Detective Glodi, went to the address. Detective You carefully examined the address at No. 559, a three-story Western-style building along the road. To the west was the Wanfu Lane, and across the street was the Gujiazhai Garden.

Intense Shootout 162

After Detective You finished his inspection, he ordered the surrounding area to be tightly surrounded. He then led the detectives to break into the building through the main door. As they were about to go upstairs, the kidnappers upstairs had already heard the alarm and knew things were not going well. They each took out guns and resisted from the corners. Avenue Joffre was filled with the sound of gunfire, like a string of pearls. The two sides exchanged fire for over thirty shots, lasting for a quarter of an hour. The kidnappers finally surrendered and were captured. The hostage, Shen Mengyi, was safely rescued from the third floor, and escorted to the police station. Then the remaining kidnappers were searched for.

List of Kidnappers 163

The following kidnappers were captured: Zhou A’mao (23, Suzhou), Hu Lanfang (36, Sheng County), Xu A’da (29, Ningbo), Chou Huanzhang (29, Anhui), Mao Zipi (30, local), Dong Yongliang (22, Ningbo), Tao Xiaozhang (32, local), Gao A’gen (25, Zhenjiang), female kidnapper Pan Tao (23, local, also known as Tan Xiuying; jumped from the building and injured her foot during the arrest, and has been sent to Renji Hospital), and Chen Wang (22, Ningbo), totaling ten men and women. Two six-inch Browning pistols were seized (one with five live rounds, one with six live rounds), and one four-inch pistol, with five bullets. During the shootout, the legs and arms of two kidnappers, Dong Yongliang and Tao Xiaozhang, were injured. They were also taken to the French Police Station.

Apprehension of the Kidnapper Leader 164

After a strict interrogation by the police chief, the kidnappers confessed that their leader, Ma Qiaosheng (30, Wuxi), was hiding at No. 13 in the Guianli on Route Tenant de Tour. The detectives went to the address and apprehended Ma after a brief interrogation. The eleven kidnappers, including men and women, along with the hostage, were handed over to Detective You for investigation. According to the hostage, since being kidnapped, the kidnappers had treated him relatively well in the den, prohibiting him from going downstairs or looking out the window. He was only allowed to sit or lie down on the bed. A Ningbo man with a Cantonese appearance, who worked as a cook, delivered three meals a day. This kidnapper has not yet been apprehended.

Farmer Kills Wife and Chops Her into Eleven Pieces 165

丨Out of Rage for Wife's Infidelity丨

Gu Futao, a resident of Baiyangzhai, a village on the border of Baoshan County north of Wusong, was quite fierce. He was 31 years old and worked as a stone mason. Two months ago, he spent 80 yuan to buy a woman surnamed Hu from Nanhui as his wife. However, although she was ordinary in appearance, she was extremely flirtatious and unwilling to be a farmer's wife, often going out and staying overnight under various pretexts. Futao repeatedly tried to persuade her, but she did not listen, causing him to hate her deeply. A murderous intent arose in him. Late the night before last, while Hu was fast asleep, Futao suddenly grabbed a sharp axe and chopped at Hu's head several times, killing her instantly. He then used a wooden bucket to chop Hu's body into eleven pieces, including one piece for the head, one for the chest, one for the abdomen, and four pieces each for the arms and feet. He put the pieces in the bucket and hid it in the wall. After the incident, he kept it a secret. Yesterday morning, Futao and his mother, Wang, prepared luggage and bedding, intending to flee. However, a neighbor saw Futao acting慌张 and questioned Wang, who revealed the whole story. The neighbor then arrested Futao and his mother, Wang, and handed them over to the Baoshan County government for detention. County Magistrate Jin personally went to inspect and emptied the body from the wooden bucket. The inspection was a gruesome sight. The abdomen was completely exposed with all the internal organs. The body was exposed to the hot sun, and the stench was overwhelming. The sight made onlookers nauseous, and the road was blocked.

French Mail Ship Aramis Arrives in Shanghai, First Unloading Cargo 167

Will Proceed to Nagasaki Shipyard in Japan for Repairs

Two French Warships Escorting Her Return to Original Defense Post

The Aramis, a French mail ship from the French Postal Company's Marseilles route, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday after hitting a reef in the waters off Putuo, Zhejiang Province, on the 23rd of last month. It will be unloaded and will proceed to Japan for repairs in the shipyard. The details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai and Unloading 168

The passengers' luggage and mail on the Aramis have been transported to Shanghai by the Shanghai company's De Feng Shipping Company barges. As for the two "Bans" and the engineers and workers from the Qiuxin Factory, they will first repair the breached part of the fourth cargo hold on the mail ship. After the initial repairs were completed on June 30th, it sailed to Shanghai. It arrived in Shanghai at 6 p.m. on the same day and berthed at the China Merchants Bureau Wharf in Pudong. Over 3,400 pieces of cargo shipped to Shanghai from France were unloaded and are being unloaded.

Sailing to Japan for Repairs 169

After the mail ship arrived in Shanghai, the two French warships berthed alongside, the Bellimaux and Argonaute, simultaneously sailed back to their original defense posts. After the two "Bans" from the Shanghai French Postal Company arrived in Shanghai, they consulted on the matter of entering the shipyard for repairs. However, as none of the shipyards in Shanghai could accommodate the 24,000-ton mail ship for repairs, it was decided that after the ship unloaded its cargo, it would sail to Nagasaki, Japan, to enter the shipyard for repairs.

丨Result of Explanation by the International Trade Bureau丨

Full discussions were held on the development of trade between the two countries. Considering that China's ham exports to the Philippines were substantial annually, but the Philippine authorities, not understanding the production methods, suspected uncleanness and therefore refused import, the bureau explained the production methods to the delegation and requested them to explain and lift the ban to the Philippine authorities after returning to their country. According to Guo Weibai, the chief of the General Affairs Department of the bureau, after the Philippine inspection delegation returned and reported, the ban on ham exports to the Philippines has been lifted. The people of the Philippines have always liked to eat this ham, so with the ban now lifted, the foreign trade of ham should be able to restore previous trade figures.

County Government Investigates Long-Term Brokerage Tax 177

The Shanghai County Government, citing Article 2 of the Regulations for Recognizing Brokerage Taxes in Various Counties, which stipulates that the recognized amount of brokerage tax is limited to the short term, while long-term registered business taxes and cocoon post taxes are still handled by the county governments or finance bureaus, has noted that the county finance bureau has now been merged into the county government. Therefore, with regard to long-term brokerage licenses, whether there are substitutions or replacements, or whether old licenses are being fraudulently used multiple times, officials should be dispatched to investigate to verify the facts. Therefore, County Magistrate Cao has specially appointed Commissioner He Shanqing to go to various brokers to conduct thorough investigations. In addition to separately issuing letters to the municipal and county public security bureaus yesterday, ordering them to assist at any time, he also sent letters to the municipal chamber of commerce and ordered the county chambers of commerce to inform the various brokers.

Accusation of Soviet Aid Association Employee is Purely International Politics 180

Association employee unable to fulfill major tasks

Fearing being killed upon returning to his country, he fled to Hankou, leading to the association's lawsuit

Alexander Maurisson, a Russian and the director of the chemical supplies department of the Soviet Aid Association at 2 Beijing Road, was recently sued by the association's manager, Maierkov, for embezzling 25,000 yuan. The First Special Court has already acquitted Maurisson. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. However, the occurrence of this case has a political background. At the time, neither party mentioned it, so it was impossible to record. Now, after several days of investigation by the reporter, the truth of this case has been largely clarified. The facts are recorded below.

It is found that the Soviet Aid Association is nominally the general agency for Soviet trade in China, but in reality, it is the Chinese branch of the Political Defense Bureau of Moscow in the Soviet Union. It investigates all important political matters and also engages in commerce. In January of last year, Maurisson was appointed by the Economic Department of the Russian Political Defense Bureau as the director of the chemical supplies department of the association. He actually had a major mission, which was divided into the following points: (1) Investigate the political and economic situation of the whole of China, especially paying attention to Jiangsu Province. (2) Investigate the current situation of the Kuomintang, the number of party members, and its economic situation. (3) How many times did Wang Jingwei, the president of the Executive Yuan of our country, come to Shanghai, where did he live, who was responsible for his protection, how many Chinese and Western patrolmen were there, where did he eat, and who prepared the food? Because the Soviet Union hated Wang more than Chiang. (4) Investigate the internal conflicts of the central government and the Sino-Japanese issue, the conflicts and propositions of government personnel. (5) Investigate the Chinese who defected from the Communist Party and surrendered to the Kuomintang, and what kind of news they leaked, etc. However, after Mao came to Shanghai, he felt that he was being monitored and it was not easy to move around, so he failed to do his best to investigate the mission, which led to a reprimand from the National Defense Bureau. Maierkov was dispatched to Shanghai to work in place of Mao. After Mai came to Shanghai, he organized an active working committee, of which Mao was also a member. However, because Mao was under severe surveillance everywhere, he still failed to achieve any results, and his views differed from those of Mai. As a result, Mai wanted to send Mao back to Moscow. Mao, considering that there had been a case of Ge Lingfei, who was also sent back to Russia and then shot, did not dare to return to Russia, but he also did not dare to stay in Shanghai, so he secretly left Shanghai and went to Hankou to avoid his edge. Unexpectedly, Maierkov, fearing that he would divulge the secrets, sued him for embezzlement to stop his mouth. Mao heard about it in Hankou and immediately returned to Shanghai with lawyer Qiu Fenling to turn himself in. After the trial judge inquired and clarified, he acquitted him. However, the police stated that they still needed to consider whether to appeal, so he was ordered to post bail and be released during the appeal period. It is now heard that the police may withdraw the appeal. Whether this is true remains to be verified.

Truth about the Sheng'an Steamer Massacre 181

Purely a Murder Driven by Adultery and Revenge

Previous Reports of Robbery Were Inaccurate

The incident of the Sheng'an Steamer of the China-Foreign Steamer Company encountering a robbery and a massacre has been recorded in yesterday's news. After a thorough investigation by this reporter, it was learned that the facts were wrong. It was the Sheng'an Steamer of the Tianjin Zhidong Company, and it was a murder driven by revenge rather than a robbery. The truth of the matter is detailed below.

Sheng'an Transports Coal to Fujian 182

The Tianjin Zhidong Steamer Company was founded by Mr. Sheng Kunshan and has many seagoing vessels operating between Shanghai and various ports in North China. Last year, it purchased a new seagoing vessel with a capacity of 1,700 tons, which was named Sheng'an. Initially, no passenger seats were sold inside the ship. It was specially used to transport cargo for customers. This time, it loaded 1,600 tons of coal in Tianjin, which was to be directly transported to Fujian. It left Tianjin on the 26th, and a major tragedy occurred on the 28th.

Five Russians as Passengers 183

The shipowner of the Sheng'an Steamer was a Russian named Vikmeng, and the first mate was also a Russian. When the ship set sail, it did not carry passengers as a rule. However, the shipowner had five acquaintances (also White Russians) who came to the ship and asked Vikmeng to allow them to travel to Fujian Province. The shipowner allowed them, breaking the rule, because he was on good terms with the five people. He allowed five passenger seats on the left and right of the shipowner's room to go to Fuzhou on the same ship.

The Truth of the Massacre 184

When the Sheng'an Steamer sailed out of Dagu Port and reached Bohai Bay on the 28th, the five Russians who boarded the ship took advantage of the shipowner and first mate, A Shiliufu, etc., who were working, and unexpectedly drew their pistols and bombarded the two. After the shipowner and first mate were shot, they still blew the whistle, and the first mate's wife heard the sound and came out to see what was happening, and she was also shot and killed. At that time, there were four Chinese helmsmen, one Chinese steward, and one wireless telegraphy trainee inside the ship. They heard the whistle and went to the shipowner's room to see what was happening, but the five murderers each fired their pistols and killed the seven crew members, including the helmsmen, steward, and wireless telegraphy trainee.

The Murderers Confessed to the Assassination 185

The five murderers, seeing that the shipowner, first mate, etc., had been killed and the purpose had been achieved, declared to the second mate, the engineers, and all the crew members on the ship that the shipowner and first mate had a great hatred for them. The cause was due to a rivalry for love. Today's murder was entirely to avenge personal grievances and had no other purpose. As for the killing of the helmsmen and steward, it was because they interfered and helped the shipowner, so they were killed together. They ordered everyone not to be afraid. After the statement, they ordered the sailors to throw the ten corpses of the shipowner, etc., into the sea to destroy them.

The Ship Ran Aground en Route 186

After the tragedy occurred, the shipowner was dead, and the responsibility for the entire ship was transferred to the second mate. At that time, after discussion with the crew members, it was decided to head to the nearest port. As a result, Dalian was the closest to the location, so they set off immediately. That night, the weather was very bad. When the Sheng'an Steamer was sailing in the Xingpu Sea area, it ran aground on a reef due to a mistaken navigation route. The bottom of the ship was broken by the reef and lost its ability to move. Therefore, the second mate decided to send a telegram to the head office for help, and at the same time, they tried to repair the hole on the ship and drain the accumulated water to prevent it from sinking.

The Murderers Fled and Were Captured 187

The five murderers took advantage of the ship's accident and each released a sampan to flee towards Dalian. After the crew members left the ship, they sent a telegram to Dehang to report the tragedy of the shipowner's murder. Later, it was heard that after the five murderers arrived in Dalian, three of them had been arrested by the Japanese police, and two were still at large and were still being searched for. Zhidong Company received the report and immediately telegraphed the Dalian branch to first send a tugboat with workers and pumps to Xingpu to tow and rescue the Sheng'an Steamer. According to the person in charge of the company, the murderers were indeed Russians, and it was purely a murder driven by adultery and revenge. Now that the Sheng'an has run aground, it is hoped that it can be pulled out. Tianjin Dehang will separately appoint a shipowner and first mate to the ship to investigate the murderers. There were no other passengers on board. In addition to coal, no other cargo was loaded.

Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly

A Bird's-Eye View of Shanghai's Medicine and Pharmacy in the Last Decade (Continued) 199

— Pang Jingzhou

Chapter 5: Administration of Medicine and Pharmacy

Section 2: Names and Organizations in the Medical and Pharmaceutical Fields

Besides these are the learned societies. Currently, the headquarters of two major societies are in Shanghai: the Chinese Medical Association and the Medical and Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China. There was also the former "Bo Yi Hui" (Medical Society), organized by Western missionaries and Chinese people, which has now been merged into the Chinese Medical Association. Originally, the nature of a learned society is different from that of a guild; the former is an academic institution, while the latter is a professional organization. However, in reality, before the establishment of a physicians' guild, all external negotiations and internal self-governance of the medical community relied on the unity of these two learned societies. Furthermore, physicians' guilds have the nature of local units. If a place has a small number of people and cannot establish a guild, they can still enjoy the rights of the learned society's headquarters. Therefore, learned societies have always had connections with medical administration. In my opinion, in the near future, there will inevitably be a grand alliance of various medical societies, with one part discussing medicine and another part studying medical administration and business.

In the field of new pharmaceuticals, initially, there was simply no specific name because China had no specialized pharmacy discipline. It was only after the graduates of pharmaceutical schools appeared that the term "pharmacist" gradually emerged. However, their numbers were small, and no independent organization was established. Therefore, most of the talents in the pharmaceutical field were members of the Medical and Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China. Later, it was felt that the trend of the times dictated that medicine and pharmacy should be separated. Therefore, most of the members voluntarily formed the Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China. In addition to the learned society, a pharmacists' guild has recently been established, as well as a so-called New Pharmaceutical Society. The details are not very clear.

In terms of pharmacies and merchants, there is a New Pharmaceutical Industry Guild, which was advocated by Mr. Huang Chujiu in those years. Although it was not possible to get all pharmacies to join at the time, it was a very good form of unity. Among the pharmacies, there were also some apprentice-trained dispensing pharmacists who, motivated by a strict order from the Ministry of Health, voluntarily organized a Dispensing Pharmacists' Guild, which was unrelated to both pharmacy merchants and pharmacy academics. In fact, they can be called necessary pharmaceutical workers.

In the field of traditional medicine, the earliest organization was called the Shenzhou Medical and Pharmaceutical Society, which was established by Mr. Li Pingshu in Japan. He once served as its president. The nature of this society was also a mix of learned society and guild. Now, the most fashionable organization is called the Guoyi Guan (National Medicine Hall), and its tone is grand. Firstly, its birthplace is the Central Party Headquarters, not an organization voluntarily formed by doctors. Secondly, it has the support of important figures, so its nature is like a research institute, and also like a general association of old medical societies; and also like a university. Recently, it has also wanted to seize the right to manage the practice of old medicine, which makes it seem like the Ministry of Interior's Department of Health. Unfortunately, this almighty Guoyi Guan does not form a cohesive whole with the original old medical organizations, so that its almightiness is equal to its ineffectiveness, and it does nothing. There was originally no independent discipline in the field of old medicine, only drug merchants, so there was no academic unity, only commercial guilds, which are the trade associations of traditional Chinese medicine shops and old medicine merchants. Although shop assistants and old stewards (i.e., pharmaceutical manufacturers) did not have a guild, they had a labor union. I remember that there was a strike over the issue of wage increases the year before last, and pharmacies also went on strike.

Discussion on Pulse Diagnosis at the Cun Kou (3) 200

— Yu Yunxiu

(6) The section on the two sides within the "chi" in the Su Wen cannot be grafted onto the Cun Kou pulse method

In the "Pulse Essence and Subtle Theory" of the Su Wen, there is a section that says: "The two sides within the chi are the hypochondria. The outer chi is used to observe the kidneys, the inner chi is used to observe the abdomen. The middle part is attached above. The outer left is used to observe the liver, the inner to observe the diaphragm. The outer right is used to observe the stomach, the inner to observe the spleen, attached above. The outer right is used to observe the lungs, the inner to observe the chest. The outer left is used to observe the heart, the inner to observe the Tan Zhong. The front is used to observe the front, the back is used to observe the back. The top of the upper part concerns the chest and throat. The bottom of the lower part concerns the lower abdomen, waist, thighs, knees, shins, and feet." This section of text seems close to the Cun Kou pulse method. After the Jin and Yuan dynasties, the trend of reviving ancient ways was very strong, so the people of the Ming Dynasty all attached the section of text from the Su Wen to the Cun Kou pulse method, believing it to be the legitimate lineage passed down from the Yellow Emperor and Qibo. However, no one has ever been able to explain this section of text clearly. It says both "the two sides within the chi" and "the inner and outer chi." What exactly do the words "inner" and "outer" mean? Wang Qixuan, Yang Shangshan, Ma Xuantai, Zhang Yinan, and others all said that they are the two sides of the pulse. Wang Xingu, Li Zhongzi, Zhang Jingyue, Xue Shengbai, and others all said that they are the upper and lower halves of each part. The Medical Sect Golden Mirror refutes their claims, saying: "The pulse image is unified, not in two strips, nor in two sections." This statement is certainly a good refutation. However, his own claim that inner and outer are floating and sinking is wrong. He says that the pulse image is unified, but he does not think that dividing it into the cun, guan, and chi sections has already turned it into three sections. If pure sinking can be diagnosed in each place, wouldn't it become two layers again? What is he still talking about the unified pulse image? Isn't this contradicting himself? Therefore, Liao Ping of Sichuan believed that this section of text in the Su Wen was wrong no matter how he thought about it, so he changed the character "chi" to the character "foot," saying that it refers to the three parts and nine positions of the whole body, not the three parts and nine positions of the Cun Kou pulse method. Although Mr. Liao's saying is not necessarily the true meaning of the Su Wen, it shows that it is impossible to graft this section of text from the Su Wen onto the pulse method of the three parts and nine positions of the Cun Kou. The old doctors of today like to use this section of text as a talisman for the Cun Kou pulse method, saying that it is the proper method of the Yellow Emperor and Qibo. This kind of error is due to not studying ancient books carefully. They should be asked to read books behind closed doors for a few more years.

(7) The opinions of various people on the division of the viscera and bowels are different, and it is impossible to tell who is right and who is wrong

There are two major schools of thought on the pulse method of dividing the Cun Kou to observe the viscera. Before the Ming Dynasty, most people followed the words of the Pulse Classic. After the Ming Dynasty, most people grafted on the sayings of the Su Wen. However, there are many different opinions among them. For example, Chu Yong in "Dispelling Doubts" quoted the words of Chu Cheng's "Honoring Life Classic," saying that Yongzi's right chi is the Mingmen, the right guan is the spleen, the right cun is the lung, the left chi is the kidney, the left guan is the liver, the left cun is the heart; for women, the left cun is the Mingmen, the left guan is the spleen, the left chi is the lung, the right cun is the kidney, the left guan is the liver, and the right chi is the heart. The Pulse Classic says that the left belongs to the kidney, and the right is the Zihu, called the Sanjiao. Hua Boren said that the left chi is the kidney, bladder, and Mingmen, the right chi is the Sanjiao and pericardium. Zhu Danxi said that the left chi is the kidney and bladder, and the right chi is the Mingmen and Sanjiao; Li Shimai said that the left chi is the kidney and bladder, and the right chi is the kidney and large intestine; Li Yan said that the Mingmen is on the left for men and on the right for women; Xu Chunfu said that the left chi diagnoses the small intestine and bladder, and the right chi diagnoses the large intestine; Yu Jiayan said that the small intestine should be observed on the right chi, and the large intestine should be observed on the left chi; Zhang Jingyue said that the left cun observes the heart and pericardium, the right cun observes the lungs and Zhongshu, the left chi observes the kidney, bladder, and large intestine, and the right chi observes the kidney, Sanjiao, Mingmen, and small intestine; Chen Wuzhi said that the viscera observe external affections, and the bowels observe internal injuries; Li Dongyuan said that the left governs external affections, and the right governs internal injuries. Looking at the claims of the various families mentioned above, almost no one has the same opinion. If there is right and wrong, A argues with B. Whose words are correct in the end? Therefore, Chen Xiuyuan was at a loss and randomly listed the words of the Su Wen, Wang Shenghe, Li Binhu, and Zhang Jingyue, saying that they all made sense and could only be used together. Ladies and gentlemen, please think about it. There is only one truth. How can the learning of each family be compatible and inclusive? Is it possible to adopt an ambiguous, gray attitude of mixing right and wrong? Can this kind of technique be really applied to diagnosing diseases and be able to recognize the true face of the disease? It is truly confused and ridiculous!

(8) Old doctors say that the beating of the pulse is all "qi"

The "Ordinary People's Qi Image Theory" of the Su Wen says: "The major Luo of the stomach is called the Xu Li, which runs through the diaphragm and connects with the lungs, emerging below the left breast. Its movement responds to clothing. It is the source of the pulse qi." The thing inside under the left breast is the tip of the heart. Its beating is the beating of the heart, which is the driving force of all arterial pulsations. Saying that it is "the source of the pulse" is correct. Saying that it is "qi" is wrong. Saying that it is "the major Luo of the stomach" is even more wrong. Roughly speaking, the ancients thought that the beating of the pulse was all qi. I can use the words of the "Fifty Ying" of the Ling Shu to prove it. It says, "When a person exhales, the pulse beats twice, and the qi travels three inches. When a person inhales, the pulse also beats twice, and the qi travels three inches. When breathing is stable, the pulse travels six inches... After two hundred and seventy breaths, it travels sixteen zhang and two chi... Around the body, two ke of water fall... After thirteen thousand five hundred breaths, the qi travels fifty ying in the body." This is the evidence that the ancients mistook the beating of the pulse for the flow of qi. Even now, your country's doctors still regard the pulse as qi. For example, Li Binhu, he already knows that the pulse of the Cun Kou is not the location of the viscera, but he still regards the pulse as the qi of the viscera. Other doctors also have the same view. Isn't that a big mistake?

The Entrance Examination System and Students' Health Problems 201

— Song Guobin

In the past, I published an article entitled "Education and Health," stating that the current education system is very harmful to the health of young people. For example, too many exams, too much curriculum, poor diet, and cramped living conditions are all related to the health of students. Therefore, neurasthenia has become a prevalent disease in schools. This is nothing more than the exams and curriculum not being appropriate. Medicine and education are deeply related. When it comes to health, doctors have a responsibility to speak out. I would like to use this idea to discuss today's entrance examination system. Exams are the most burdensome thing in a student's life, and this is especially true in our country. There are exams every ten days, exams every month, exams every semester, and exams upon graduation. Almost half of the time in a year is spent on exams, and almost half of the students' bodies are injured due to too many exams. The graduation exam is especially bad. The need to improve the examination system is undeniable. Now, please let me talk about the relationship between the entrance examination and health as follows:

First, the overcrowding of people in the city.

Holding graduation exams in the heat of summer or the cold of winter is already detrimental to the health of children. However, it is difficult to change the established rules, and at the time of the exam, it is only one school, and the number of students is not too large, which is still acceptable. Now, the schools in the area are gathered together in one hall, and the poor air quality and cramped buildings are self-evident. In addition, among the students, not all of them are completely healthy. Some have not recovered from their illnesses, and some have infectious diseases that have not passed the infectious period (such as diphtheria and scarlet fever). All of them have to come because of the entrance examination, and the spread of germs is about to break out. The more people there are, the more the infection spreads. How can the danger be measured? This is one.

Second, the hardship of traveling back and forth.

The entrance examination means that students from various schools are gathered in one place. If there is a gathering place, then there is a difference between the distance between the students and the examination hall. It goes without saying for those who are close, but those who are far away have to run around in the scorching sun. Can middle school students who are not yet adults bear this? Moreover, the examination period is not just one day; what is examined in a day is not just one time. The journey back and forth is enough to exhaust them, and as for diet, there is even no way to take it into account! This is two.

Third, the schools are opening up fast trains.

Schools that have always advocated laissez-faire will inevitably be at a loss when they suddenly hear the order for the entrance examination, and they will have no way to hide their clumsiness. If the school authorities want to maintain the school's reputation, then it is difficult to take care of the students' suffering. They have no choice but to think of the next best thing, which is to speed up the curriculum and open up the fast train without stopping, regardless of whether the students can accept it. Students who have received laissez-faire education on weekdays are now subjected to coercive measures. Those who are eager to win will forget to eat and sleep, while those who are timid will become lazy due to fear. Since the clear order for the entrance examination was issued, the number of middle and primary school students who have contracted neurasthenia due to excessive study has increased day by day. This is three.

The above is just a rough outline. As for other things that are not related to health, such as teachers privately stealing exam questions with students, students cheating on the spot, and the larger the scope, the more the disadvantages. With health as the center of education, is this not what the education authorities of this city have been proclaiming to us? However, on the one hand, they talk about children's health in order to achieve healthy education, while on the other hand, they carry out the entrance examination system, which is a government policy that destroys children's health, and they are afraid that it will not be carried out. Is there any contradiction greater than this? Therefore, I am not surprised that this kind of government order was issued, but I am surprised that it was issued at a time when the world is promoting healthy education, and the central health authorities have no objection. I am not surprised that this kind of government order can be implemented, but I am surprised that the first place to implement it is the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, which takes health as the center of education, and the municipal health authorities also have no objection. Therefore, I would like to express my views briefly for those who are concerned about this issue to read!

Scientific Methods of Nurturing Life (23) 202

— Yu Songyun

(19) Health Preservation During Childbirth

(A) The Necessity of Hygiene

After childbirth, when you are at ease and have nothing to do, you should rest your mind and recuperate. No matter what, you must take hygiene as the premise. The six-week postpartum period requires considerable health preservation, which is actually more important than the ten months of pregnancy.

If you do not take care of your health during childbirth, it often leads to unfortunate consequences, and it is easy to ruin your life. For example, puerperal fever, uterine retroversion, infertility, endometritis, salpingitis, and other diseases are mostly caused by unhygienic conditions, especially puerperal fever, which is very easy to occur.

(B) Body Cleansing

During childbirth, there is night sweat secretion, messy juice overflow, underarm staining, and lochia discharge. Therefore, the whole body is unclean. In addition to local washing within the possible range, you must wait four weeks before taking a bath to seek complete cleanliness. Clothes and bedding must be loose, clean, and soft. Pads and mattresses should also be soft and warm, and should be replaced and washed frequently. The room should have sufficient light and air circulation, and direct sunlight and direct ventilation should be prevented. Also, the filth of lochia, the cleaning of bedpans, the cleaning of furniture, and the cleaning of the four corners should all be kept as clean as possible.

(C) Bowel Movements and Urination

It is often easy to become constipated after childbirth. This is because the function of intestinal peristalsis is slow and the internal pressure of the intestinal cavity decreases. Although constipation for three days after childbirth is not a major problem, prolonged constipation is harmful to the mind and body. A gentle laxative method should be used. Enemas with warm water, soapy water, or glycerin can be used first. If it is still ineffective, then laxatives such as Glauber's salt, magnesium sulfate, or castor oil can be administered. However, rhubarb should not be used because it can be transferred to breast milk.

Urination is generally difficult after childbirth. Excessive bladder filling hinders uterine contraction, so urination should not be accumulated for too long. If there is no urination within six hours, warm, moist cloths can be applied to the bladder area. Or massage and compress the bladder area, or use sterilized cold water to irrigate the urethral opening in order to promote the urge to urinate. If it is still ineffective, then use a catheter to perform catheterization, but all sterilization should be even more rigorous than usual, otherwise lochia will enter the bladder and you will suffer a lot!

Common Sense About Diseases: Questions and Answers 203

— Cheng Hanzhang

(9) Cholera (Vomiting and Diarrhea Epidemic)

Q: What methods can be used to treat cramps in the calf and thigh muscles? A: Warm, moist cloths can be applied to the area, or chloroform oil can be used for rubbing. Alcohol can also be used for rubbing.

Q: What are the prevention methods for cholera?

A: Isolate patients, suspected patients, and carriers. All patient utensils and excreta must be disinfected. Be careful not to eat food and drinks sold on the street, drive away flies, and be careful with your diet to avoid harming your stomach and intestines. Inject cholera prevention vaccine. Q: What is the so-called "epidemic prevention injection" and how is it injected? A: It is the cholera vaccine, which should be injected at the beginning of summer. It is generally divided into three injections: the first injection is 500 million dead bacteria, and the second and third injections are both 1 billion. Inject once a week to enable the body to develop the ability to resist bacteria. However, what is commonly injected now is a mixed vaccine for cholera and typhoid fever, which is also divided into three injections. The first injection is half a cc (1 billion dead cholera bacteria and 250 million dead typhoid bacteria), and the second injection is 1 cc.

(10) Intestinal Fever (Typhoid Fever) (Part 1)

Q: How does intestinal fever start?

A: Intestinal fever is typhoid fever. It is caused by eating unclean food containing typhoid bacteria.

Q: What is the Western name for intestinal fever?

A: The English name is Typhoid fever, the German name is Unterleibtyphus, and the Latin name is Typhus Abdominalis.

Q: Who discovered this pathogen and what is its morphology?

A: It was discovered by Mr. Eberth and Mr. Gaffky. The morphology is a rod-shaped bacterium, the length of which is about one-third of the diameter of a red blood cell. The ends of the bacteria have flagella and can move.

Q: After the pathogens enter the intestine, what changes occur in which part?

A: They occupy and reproduce in the small intestine. At first, the intestinal tube is congested and swollen, then it becomes necrotic and forms scabs. Finally, the scabs fall off and form ulcers, and eventually scars form and it heals.

Q: After the pathogen of intestinal fever is transmitted, how many days does it take to develop the disease?

A: It takes one week to three weeks of incubation before the disease develops after infection.

Q: How does the onset of the disease begin?

A: It starts with prodromal symptoms, which are general malaise, loss of appetite, and pain in the limbs. The body feels chills, and then fever develops.

Q: What happens after that?

A: The entire course of intestinal fever can be divided into four stages: the initial stage, the extreme stage, the relaxation stage, and the remission stage. Each stage lasts for one week, for a total of four weeks.

Q: What are the symptoms of the initial stage?

A: The symptoms at this time are more obvious than those mentioned above. The fever rises daily, like a ladder, decreasing in the morning and increasing in the evening, but on average, each morning and evening is half a degree or one degree higher than the previous day. The highest temperature is reached on the fifth to seventh day. The tongue is dry and covered with thick fur, the pulse is repetitive, and there is constipation or diarrhea. In addition, due to the swelling of the spleen, there is pain in the left hypochondriac region, and roseola red spots appear on the skin of the chest and abdomen. Q: What are the symptoms of the extreme stage?

A: By the time of the extreme stage, the systemic symptoms increase, and the body temperature remains at a high fever of 39 or 40 degrees Celsius, with a difference of less than one degree between morning and evening (called sustained fever). The pulse is frequent, but it does not parallel the fever. In addition, the abdomen is full (bloating), there is rumbling in the ileocecal region, and there is tenderness to pressure, and the spleen is obviously swollen. The face has a dull appearance; it is trapped in drowsiness and coma, and delirium occurs from time to time. There is often a cough.

Q: What are the symptoms of the relaxation stage?

A: The temperature begins to show a high and low relaxation state. The degree is gradually clear. At the end of this stage, the roseola completely disappears, and miliaria (commonly known as "white deafness") appears. The tongue coating peels off and there is some appetite. In severe patients, complications of heart failure are the most dangerous, especially intestinal bleeding, intestinal perforation, or catarrhal pneumonia.

Q: Are these complications fatal?

A: Yes. The death of intestinal fever patients is mostly due to several complications at this time.

Q: What are the symptoms of the remission stage?

A: The relaxation state of the temperature in this stage is even more obvious, with a difference of more than two degrees between morning and evening. Finally, it becomes intermittent and decreases in a scattered state. The swelling of the spleen and bloating disappear, and it enters the recovery period. (To be continued)

New Explanation of "Paralysis and Abdominal Distension" (3) 204

— Hu Jiayan

(2) Abdominal Distension

The mention of abdominal distension inevitably brings to mind what we call ascites. I believe it can almost entirely represent ascites. Its causes generally fall into the following three categories: (1) it is one of the local symptoms of impaired blood circulation in the lungs due to heart disease; (2) it is a result of edema caused by nephritis; (3) it is caused by impaired portal blood flow, leading to fluid accumulation in the abdominal cavity, mostly due to liver diseases. Atrophic cirrhosis and liver syphilis are the most prominent examples. In addition, various diseases of the peritoneum can sometimes occur, with tuberculous peritonitis being a good example. Ovarian hydrops in women can sometimes be difficult to distinguish from ascites, and it is naturally included in abdominal distension. People generally believe that there are two types of abdominal distension: fluid distension and gas distension. The former refers to ascites, while the latter refers to any abdominal distension caused by gas accumulation in the abdomen. There are many examples of this type, such as tuberculous peritonitis, which can resemble it when exudate solidifies into connective tissue. Children with intestinal parasitic infections can also exhibit this symptom.

Based on the above, the generally recognized disease of abdominal distension can be attributed to the following conditions in our new medical understanding: atrophic cirrhosis, liver syphilis, ovarian hydrops, heart disease, nephritis, and tuberculous peritonitis. The specific symptoms of each disease will now be described separately below:

(1) Atrophic Cirrhosis

This condition initially manifests as digestive disorders, a feeling of pressure in the stomach, and occasional bloating in the abdomen. Later, the complexion gradually becomes pale and gray, with mild jaundice in the eyes. The liver initially appears enlarged but gradually shrinks, while the spleen becomes enlarged. The main symptoms are ascites and varicose veins in the abdomen, which are the basis for diagnosing this condition. This condition is often caused by chronic alcohol poisoning, but it is also not uncommon after acute infectious diseases. Treatment includes abstaining from alcohol and other stimulants. If syphilis or malaria is the underlying cause, specific treatments for those conditions can be used. Diuretics are essential, with mercury injections being effective. However, if ascites does not subside with continued injections, paracentesis can be used to drain the fluid. However, the distension is likely to recur after drainage, requiring multiple procedures to be effective. The prognosis for this condition is poor. Once the symptoms are fully apparent (ascites is present), the lifespan is generally no more than two to three years. The condition can sometimes be life-threatening due to massive hematemesis, similar to gastric ulcer.

(2) Liver Syphilis

This condition is one of the symptoms of tertiary syphilis. Rubber-like masses develop in the liver, ranging in size from millet grains to walnuts, white or reddish-gray in color, mostly on the surface of the liver, but also occasionally in the portal area. The symptoms resemble those of atrophic cirrhosis. There are generally no subjective symptoms. Ascites, splenomegaly, and hepatomegaly are the most prominent features, similar to hypertrophic cirrhosis. However, there are occasional episodes of biliary colic-like pain, accompanied by hectic fever. Jaundice may also occur. The course of this condition is chronic, and the prognosis is poor. In addition to specific anti-syphilitic treatment, symptomatic treatment is the same as before.

(3) Ovarian Hydrops

This is one of the women's diseases. The external appearance of the abdomen is almost identical to ascites, with no specific subjective symptoms. Differentiation requires abdominal paracentesis to examine the fluid. The fluid in common ascites is mostly transparent, containing white blood cells, red blood cells, and a small amount of protein, with a specific gravity below 1.012. The fluid in this condition is darker, viscous, and contains columnar epithelial cells with cilia, sometimes with serous fluid. The protein content can reach 5%, and the specific gravity can be above 1.020. Treatment involves surgical excision, which can be curative. However, the prognosis is less favorable for those with serous fluid.

(4) Cardiac Edema

Chronic endocarditis causes congestion, leading to blood leakage and accumulation in tissues, resulting in edema. It initially appears in the feet and scrotum, and later presents as ascites and skin edema. It is also seen in hydropericardium. Patients experience difficulty breathing, are unable to lie supine, have reduced urine output, and sometimes exhibit proteinuria. In addition to digitalis preparations, diuretics are very helpful, and mercury preparations can also be used. For those with syphilitic origin, iodine-bismuth preparations can be injected. It is sometimes not difficult to reduce or eliminate ascites and skin edema in this condition. However, the underlying heart disease is difficult to cure completely. The prognosis is better for those caused by syphilis.

(5) Nephritis

This condition often occurs after acute infectious diseases such as scarlet fever and typhoid fever. The main symptom is decreased urine output, with a minimum of only 200 cubic centimeters (200 cc) per day. The urine is dark brown, cloudy, and contains a large amount of protein, red blood cells, white blood cells, renal epithelial tissue, and various types of casts. There are occasional symptoms of fever and tenderness in the kidney area. Edema initially appears around the eyes, gradually spreading to both feet, then to the scrotum, and finally to ascites, pleural effusion, and the whole body, unlike cardiac edema, which initially appears in both feet. The course of this condition generally leads to one of three outcomes: complete recovery, chronic nephritis, or death from uremia. Treatment initially requires abstaining from salt, and fluid intake must also be restricted. When edema has not subsided, consuming only milk is best, up to two liters per day. Diuretics should be used with caution, and mercury injections should be prohibited (to avoid excessive stimulation of the kidneys and intestines). Diaphoretics and radiant heat baths are best for reducing swelling. If this condition does not become chronic and the patient follows the doctor's instructions regarding diet during the treatment period, complete recovery is generally possible.

(6) Tuberculous Peritonitis

This condition is caused by the invasion of the peritoneum by tuberculosis bacteria. It is more common in children and adolescents. The changes can be miliary tuberculosis, mass formation, or ascites. The ascitic fluid is dark brown, serofibrinous, sometimes with bleeding or hemorrhagic purulent properties. The specific gravity is usually above 1.005, and the protein content is also high, which is different from liver diseases. The main symptoms are abdominal distension, abdominal wall rigidity, and abdominal tenderness. Occasional low-grade fever and poor appetite are also present. The course of this condition ranges from several months to several years. The prognosis is better than other forms of tuberculosis, with occasional complete cures. If diagnosis is difficult, peritoneal puncture can be performed. In addition to general tuberculosis treatment, applying Sapo Kallnus and using a sun lamp can also be effective. Because intestinal adhesion to the abdominal wall is common in this condition, paracentesis should be performed with caution. Surgical intervention is only suitable for exudative forms, but not when there is tuberculosis in the intestines or lungs, or when there is fever.

In addition to the above conditions, edematous and acute malignant beriberi, when edema gradually spreads throughout the body, are also generally regarded as abdominal distension. Even intestinal parasitic infections in children, when the abdomen is distended, are sometimes mistaken. However, these two conditions are easily distinguishable by doctors and are less likely to occur, so I will not elaborate further here!

Now I can answer the question of whether the prognosis for abdominal distension is good or bad! Of the conditions mentioned above, atrophic cirrhosis has the least hope, followed by liver syphilis. The other conditions are all very promising. There are many examples of cures. Take endocarditis as an example. It is undeniable that valvular insufficiency and stenosis cannot be cured, but systemic edema can be eliminated. Subjective symptoms can sometimes be absent. Even regarding recurrence, there is great hope as long as the patient takes proper care of themselves. It depends entirely on whether the patient has a deep understanding of their condition! Regarding the issue of draining ascites by paracentesis, many people are very dissatisfied because the distension recurs after drainage. We have never concealed the fact that this procedure is not a specific cure, but it is the only reliable way to eliminate ascites today and is a powerful resistance to portal blood flow disorders. If it is continued multiple times, there is still a glimmer of hope. I hope that everyone who reads this article should deeply understand this point. (To be continued)
