Novel

Under the Red and Green Lights (16) 271

— Xi Lin

The night was quiet and still. Alone in my small room, I couldn't help but feel a sense of being lost. Because Wang Hua borrowed money, I remembered that I only had four meal tickets in my pocket, and I couldn't help but take a cold breath. "Alas... you need power, you need a crowd, then they'll be willing to give you money for books! Okay, let's do it his way." But where is our power and our crowd? His heart hung up again. Indeed, Shi Qiao had always been a lover of literature and music, especially in the past two years, busy chasing after life, and he had long been alienated from mass activities. Moreover, his arrogance made him fundamentally despise Wang Hua's so-called masses. What could he do now? Of course, the more he thought about it, the less he could come up with a result, so he gave up on himself and lay down on the bed.

In the silence, the faint, mournful sound of the pipa from Meizi's room came, which stirred up his sad mood even more. His long-forgotten old mother gradually stirred his imagination, and then his gentle childhood came to him as well. He couldn't help but feel a pang in his nose, and tears almost flowed out.

"Is this still like a young man?" He suddenly sat up, clenched his fists, and examined his tall body, from which he deduced his future and destiny.

The sound of cannons in Zhabei had been echoing day and night for many days. He went to open the window, gazing remotely at the black sky on the front line, and his blood boiled again. But the stars in the sky were still winking peacefully. He then wondered if Zhou Shaoping had reached the front line and how Zhang Honglie was doing. A gust of chilly night wind slapped his face, and he instinctively closed the window. The pipa sound of the sorrowful foreigner was still chirping a sad tune, and he suddenly felt disgusted by this weak sound – a kind of disgust that strong people have for the weak. Unexpectedly, a more violent disgust surged into his chest: the Third Aunt had returned from a drunken dance. The sound of her heels going upstairs. "These drunken dreamers! Drunken dreamers!" He resolved not to associate with this enchanting woman anymore.

That night, no matter how his thoughts and feelings changed, they ultimately converged on "How should I talk to Chen Tianren tomorrow? Ah, I have to get up early tomorrow!" And so he forced himself to sleep.

Film Supplement

New Trends in the Japanese Film Industry (Part 1) 272

— Huang Yingdai

Peculiarities of Film Censorship and the Kissing Problem

Using Film as a Tool for International Propaganda

Japanese newspapers and magazines have recently been attacking the film censorship board, saying that their censorship of films is very strict; in fact, this is not the case. In the eyes of some people, Japanese film censorship has always been very lenient in its examination of films. In Japan, when all films are reviewed, an average of three out of twenty-five frames are cut by the censorship board. But in the United States, three out of five reviewed films are cut. On this point alone, can we really criticize the Japanese film censorship board? In Japan, the film censorship board reviews roughly twenty films a day, but here we must remember a common condition, which is that the main issue they review is whether the content of the film is sufficient to affect the morals of the Japanese people. In the film, a particular segment often meets the scissors, and that is the kissing scene. In other countries, the kissing scene in a film may not always be cut. But in Japan, as long as it is a kiss, regardless of whether it harms public morals, it must be completely cut. This is because kissing is completely contrary to Japanese customs and is purely a Western etiquette. Japanese audiences will laugh wildly when they see kissing on the screen because they don't know what kissing is all about. And what the Japanese film censorship board wants to cut from foreign films is this kind of sensual kissing. As for kissing as an expression of true love, such as a husband and wife, mother-in-law and children, lovers expressing true love, the censorship board preserves and does not cut. Since the invention of sound films, a new problem has arisen. On the screen, a sound can be made when kissing, and the censorship board also cuts out kisses with sound because Japanese movie fans do not welcome this kind of kissing sound. Japanese directors sometimes adopt new methods, using women's arms around men's shoulders, or heels off the floor, both of which are ways of implying a kiss, but the censorship board also cuts these places.

However, in any case, in Japan, due to the influence of foreign films, the matter of kissing will sooner or later be allowed by the authorities. Regardless of the preferences of the censorship board or private individuals, there will eventually be a day of reality. Because Japanese people have gradually understood the true meaning of kissing recently, so in the near future, within reasonable limits, kissing will definitely be seen on the screen. But it's still impossible now! In addition, what the censorship board pays attention to is whether a film has any harm to Japan's political and social system. For this reason, Soviet films cannot be publicly screened in Japan. However, some people say that Soviet films do not suit the tastes of the Japanese, so the Japanese do not welcome them, and they are not suitable for the Japanese imagination. According to the Japanese censorship board, American films have been catering to the lower classes more and more recently, so censorship work has become increasingly difficult. (To be continued)

The Earliest Inventor of Cinema 273

According to a Trans-Pacific News Agency dispatch from Berlin, the world's first inventor of motion pictures was a German named Max Skladanowsky. He is now seventy years old, forty years after his invention, but his great name has been buried and very few people know about it. Gao Boer, the current Minister of Propaganda of Germany, knows his secrets very well; he made a special trip to visit Mr. Skladanowsky at his former residence. Seeing Mr. Skladanowsky in his old age, Mr. Gao couldn't help but feel sad. After returning, he immediately announced the news, praising his deeds, and organized a special committee to plan for Mr. Skladanowsky's future, and started a fundraising campaign. The government also intends to posthumously award a bonus to reward his功. According to reports, Mr. Skladanowsky invented the motion picture as early as 1895. On November 1 of that year, Mr. Skladanowsky registered his new invention with the government in Berlin, and on the same day, he publicly screened his motion picture in Berlin. For a time, those who saw the shadows of people on the screen coming and going were all regarded as strange and kept marveling. Unfortunately, he was trapped by his financial resources and could not continue to research. Later, those who rose up had heard the news and followed, causing Mr. Skladanowsky to be buried for decades, which is a pity.

Film Reviews

Review of "Hot-Handed Punishment of Adultery" *This Sporting Age* 274

— Ling He

Almost every American movie is the same, no matter what the story is, there must be love. Generally speaking, this film should be crowned with the title of "martial arts film," but the "fighting martial arts" scenes do not occupy a major part. On the contrary, the depiction of love is carefully shot, and the horse racing and polo scenes are just some lively insertions. Therefore, if the author of this film originally intended to focus on martial arts, it is inevitable that the secondary becomes the primary.

But since they relaxed the main theme of martial arts and focused on the depiction of love, then how is the latter depicted? I feel that as shown on the screen, there is no central depiction at all. If the protagonist, Steel, is a model character in the author's mind, such as his fairness and lack of harshness towards subordinates, then he should cherish himself for that widow. Can he kill Mallaire who has raped his daughter and not blame himself? Of course, he cannot be regarded as a "perfect person," not to mention the so-called "killing with a hidden arrow is not a hero." Then should his daughter be a model character? Yes, the author does have a consistent description of her, but is her chastity something that every audience can sympathize with? As for the love scene between the daughter and that young man, it is even more unnecessary in the play.

The above is a judgment based on the structure of the story. As for the meaning, it is completely empty.

However, the directing skills of this film are quite worth seeing in small aspects. Although the director is primarily responsible for the proper handling of the plot, especially for the contradictions in the protagonist's personality as mentioned above, he has had a great deal of success in Montage. For example, from the time the girl and the lustful man met in the dance hall to the time she was raped, the process in between is written very carefully and fully. Also, the girl's phone call to the widow's house, lightly explaining the fornication between her father and the widow, is also a very flexible trick. Furthermore, the kiss that the groom sees under the horse's feet, and the girl's initial trick to get her father away from that widow, all show intelligence. However, apart from this, the director's handling of the girl's killing scene is still not good enough. It should be the most tense scene. But it passed lightly. However, this is where he tries his best to help the actors, because it is originally difficult to perform, so he cleverly glosses over it. The last few shots of the grand reunion are unnecessary. The scenes of the girl lying ill after taking poison are all inappropriate.

In terms of performance, the protagonist, Jack Holt, is very spirited. He is the most successful in the play. Although most of the actresses who play girls are still passable, they cannot have difficult performances. The character of the lustful man is very considerate in flirting. The groom also maintained his past achievements. As for the girl's lover, he is the weakest.

Overall, this is definitely not a successful work.

Review of "Battlefield Hell" *No Man's Land* 275

— Hou Feng

A non-war film worth noting

At a time when the clouds over Asia are gathering, we cannot but attach importance to the great significance of this "Battlefield Hell" *No Man's Land* appearing on the screen. We know that films like "The Sky is the Limit" are of educational significance to the military-national people. Then, our non-war and the inspiration for peace that we give people in this "Battlefield Hell" is undoubtedly worthy of our experience and deep meaning of this non-war significance.

This "Battlefield Hell" writes about five people with different occupations, but the same is that they are living a safe and sweet life, and are swept into the hell of the battlefield by the hurricane of the First World War. Originally, these five people of different nationalities on the battlefield should be facing each other with swords and guns, but once they arrived in this hell, when everyone was struggling above the line of death, that kind of common pain and sorrow extinguished their hatred, and strongly caused them to move forward towards the road to peace with one heart and one mind under the meaning of surviving together.

The director has a "non-war determination," so every scene contains the meaning of "non-war." Although the first half of the film, which depicts the lives of those five people with different occupations, is a bit slack, the use of that kind of contrasting writing is commendable. Especially in the last scene, the five people come out of the broken trenches hand in hand, and work together to remove the barbed wire that hinders them from entering the realm of peace, thus blowing up the hell of the battlefield! This cannot but be said to be the director's cleverness.

Speaking of performance, the five people of different nationalities who are struggling on the line of death are all very good, especially the black man. Although the others do not have many performance opportunities, the "non-war" spirit is a common expression of everyone, revealed.

Therefore, we feel that although this "Battlefield Hell" cannot be regarded as a perfect film, the "non-war" significance in the present time when people are panicking about the advent of war is worth noting!

Review of "Dry Wood and Raging Fire" (*Hello Sister*) 276

— Yi Qun

Two girls longing for love, met two men hunting for beauty, met and loved, loved and met, met and quarreled, so slander, sabotage, set up meetings, turned against each other, and then came a God's favor, the house was also blown up, the woman was in crisis, the man bravely rescued, reunion. That's Dry Wood and Raging Fire!

In terms of plot and screen, "Dry Wood" and "Raging Fire" are indeed ambiguous and conform to reality. But what is the meaning? Where is the meaning? I'm ashamed to say, I don't know!

Does it expose the inequality of marriage problems under the capitalist system? Not enough! Does it describe the conflict between love and friendship? Too sloppy!

If it weren't for the American film that looked better on the screen, I really wouldn't forgive it at all!

Because: First, the story is too ordinary, second, the idea is not clear, like a conflict between love and friendship, but neither love nor friendship is established. Since Mank is so bad and Jim is so good, the two can never become close friends. If they are close friends, at least Mank, who ruins Jim's relationship with Panchi, should be someone who truly loves Panchi, but in fact, Mank is a rascal. And if Jim really loves Panchi, then he is too shallow to be angry and abandoned after hearing a few words of slander from Mank and Meili!

In short, this ordinary story is really so ordinary that it is worthless, making people feel that they cannot raise any kind of emotion after watching it, nor can they get a slightly deeper impression. Although the director desperately used raging fire. Fortunately, the director is still clever, the scenes are clear, the shots are flexible, the insertions are appropriate, and the front and back of the Montage can still make this ordinary story produce some not so ordinary pictures, and the performances of James Dunn and Zasu Pittes are also very natural. The dialogue is also interesting and clear, adding a lot of color to this film.

The Song of Songs, a Film Novel (9) 277

— Si Ping

As for Lily, Walter's kiss only aroused the impulse of the bitter ex-wife—Walter's first kiss—the enthusiasm of his arms—the change of heart in the middle of the hot love—she wondered where Walter had gone. But she is now married to Count Matzbach-Shiber! This is really incredible!

The Count received a letter from Walter, telling him that the statue he had carved for him had been completed and inviting him to attend the unveiling ceremony. The Count tore the letter to pieces. He had no heart to see the person he had bullied again. Walter felt uneasy when he saw that the Count had not arrived. He wanted to see Lily and pour out the melancholy in his heart. After losing Lily, he had no energy at work. He wondered all the time whether Lily would understand him when she saw his suicide note. He now deeply regretted that he did not have the courage at that time and easily allowed the Count to plunder his lover. He now decided to see her again.

Walter then ran to the Count's mansion. When he arrived, the Count happened to be away from home, so he led the way to see Lily. When they met, they endured it and only spoke politely. Finally, Lily vaguely uttered a few complaints, and Walter couldn't bear it anymore.

He said many words of love that he couldn't bear to part with her, walked closer to her, took her hand, and shouted, "Lily, I love you and you love me! You escape with me!"

His enthusiastic and firm sincerity touched her, so that she could no longer bear it. She had long belonged to him. The heart will never change! She asked him to wait a while. He wanted her to escape that night.

He suddenly felt that Count Matzbach was coming, so he stood up. The Count walked into the room and said "Hello" as if nothing had happened. She suppressed the hateful suspicion in her heart, deliberately welcomed Walter, and invited him to have dinner. He took the opportunity to solve this matter thoroughly. Lily and Walter were like sitting on pins and needles during dinner, and the Count joked. He said that his happiness was given by Walter, and then laughed dryly. Lily cried. She complained that Walter should not have traded her to the Count. Walter wanted to take the opportunity to tell the truth. But Lily was so angry and hateful that she didn't want to listen to him clear his name. She stood up unsteadily and pretended to have a headache, and ran to her room. (To be continued)
